Second Rent Reduction on Tianshujiao Street, MinGuo Road: Second Special Court Rules for 20% Reduction 133

From 265 yuan to 169.6 yuan. Several dozen businesses on Tianshujiao Street, MinGuo Road, in Shanghai, including Zhenhexiang Hardware Store, Guanghua Socks Factory, Yuehua Teahouse, Rongkang Electrical Supplies Store, Beiyang Barber Shop, Renchang Company, Hongyunlou Restaurant, Hansheng Company, Tongmaozhan, Hengfeng Money Exchange, Yongtaixiang, Tekang Liquor Store, and Dexing Restaurant, joined the Rent Reduction Association in 1934 and formed the Tianshujiao Street Branch to negotiate rent reduction with the landlords. In April of the same year, they reached a settlement to reduce the rent by 20%. Now, due to the deteriorating economic situation, the tenants requested a further reduction of 30%, but the landlord filed a lawsuit demanding that they vacate the premises. The tenants appealed to the Rent Reduction Association for assistance, and the association decided to file a counterclaim, entrusting the Southern District Rent Reduction Association to handle the matter. The judgment of the Jiangsu Shanghai Second Special District Court, Case No. 801 of 1935, is recorded below. The plaintiff, Heji Company's Xu Xiulu, stated that he sought a judgment ordering the defendant, Mao Lihua, to pay 1,272 yuan in rent and, if his property was insufficient to pay, that the guarantor, Zhou Zhenqing, would pay on his behalf, and also ordering the defendant to vacate the premises and bear the litigation costs, and dismissing the counterclaim. The main points of his statement were that the defendant, Mao Lihua, rented houses No. 246 and 247, MinGuo Road, from the plaintiff at a monthly rent of 212 yuan, guaranteed by Zhou Zhenqing. From August of last year to January of this year, he owed a total of six months' rent, totaling 1,272 yuan in national currency. Despite repeated reminders, he evaded payment. As for the counterclaim, the rent had already been reduced and there was a signed agreement, so there could be no further reduction and it should be dismissed. He submitted six rent receipts, one contract, one draft reminder letter, and one rent reduction agreement as evidence. The defendant, Zhenhexiang, appointed Shen Xinfu of the Southern District Rent Reduction Association as his agent, seeking a judgment dismissing the plaintiff's claim and filing a counterclaim. His defense and statement were: "It is true that the rent is owed, but it is due to the rent reduction. Money has been deposited in the bank, the rent is too high. Although it was reduced by 20% in 1934, many of the surrounding merchants still cannot survive. According to the current trend of declining property prices and land values, we now request that the rent be calculated at 70% of 212 yuan and order the defendant to pay rent accordingly." Reason: Regarding the main suit, the plaintiff requested that the defendant Mao Lihua vacate the premises because he owed six months' rent and had been sent a reminder letter. The plaintiff's reminder letter only demanded that the defendant Mao Lihua pay the full amount of rent owed within five days, which can hardly be considered as setting a reasonable deadline. It is inconsistent with the provisions of Article 440 of the Civil Code, and it is difficult to order the defendant to terminate the contract and vacate the premises. Regarding the rent owed, the defendant Mao Lihua should pay a certain amount, and the guarantor Zhou Zhenqing should bear the guarantee responsibility. The defendant's counterclaim should be examined first. Although the rent reduction agreement signed by the plaintiff on April 13, 1934, stipulated that the defendant Mao Lihua's rent would be reduced from 265 yuan to 212 yuan per month from January 1934 to 1939, there was no restriction preventing further rent reductions in the future. If the value of the rented property has declined, the tenant is entitled to claim a reduction in rent. It is now found that the value of real estate in this city has generally declined, which is a significant fact. The court, considering the circumstances and in accordance with the provisions of Article 442 of the Civil Code, believes that it should be reduced by 20%. It should be ruled that the rent of 1,272 yuan for six months should be reduced to 1,017.6 yuan, and the rent from February of this year should also be calculated at 80%, etc.

Summary of the Public Concession Health Department's Budget for the Year 137

The Public Concession Health Department's budget for this year has been drafted, reviewed and approved by the Health Committee, and submitted to the Finance Department and the Health Department for review. The main points are excerpted as follows:

Temporary Expenditure: Under the item of temporary expenditure, land and property, the original plan to purchase land in various locations for the construction of small vegetable markets, etc., has been temporarily suspended this year. However, the purchase of one and nine-tenths of a mu of land for the pig slaughterhouse on Pingliang Road, at a cost of 22,000 yuan, cannot be delayed any longer this year. In terms of housing, the remaining construction costs for the Zhaojin Road slaughterhouse of 24,500 yuan must be paid this year. The livestock feeding station urgently needs expansion this year, costing 7,000 yuan, which has also been included in the budget. In addition, there is a remaining construction cost of 9,400 yuan for the meat market cold storage, and 14,000 yuan for additional machinery and equipment, which have also been included as urgent items. Furthermore, the plans for the rooftop project and internal machinery and equipment of the slaughterhouse have been drawn up, with a total cost of 150,000 yuan, which has also been approved and included in the budget. In addition, there is a remaining construction cost of 27,000 yuan for the animal carcass disposal site, and 11,000 yuan for internal equipment, which are also pending payment and therefore included as urgent items. The hospital expenses included in the budget's temporary expenditures include 3,500 yuan for cold storage equipment at the Industrial Bureau's Isolation Hospital, as the original equipment is beyond repair and new equipment must be added. The expansion costs of the Tuberculosis Sanatorium are 8,000 yuan. According to the opinion of the head of the Public Works Department, the existing buildings of the sanatorium have many structural defects and should not be expanded further. However, in view of the current financial situation, it is not possible to purchase land and build new buildings. The number of patients with lung disease awaiting treatment is overwhelming, so the only option is to temporarily expand the sanatorium, which is expected to accommodate 50 more patients. The remaining housing costs of 6,000 yuan for the hospital laundry, and 17,000 yuan for machinery and equipment, have also been included as urgent items. In addition, the construction projects that have been temporarily suspended include the Mental Hospital and the Western District Fever Hospital, the latter of which is rumored to cost around 800,000 yuan.

Recurrent expenditure: The total amount of recurrent expenditure originally planned by the department, excluding inventory donations, subsidies, etc., listed separately, was 1,607,760 yuan, a decrease of more than 48,000 yuan compared to last year. However, the above figure is calculated based on an exchange rate of 1 shilling and 6 pence in gold per yuan in national currency. If calculated at 1 shilling and 2 and three-eighths pence, the above number would rise to 1,696,540 yuan, an increase of 50,000 yuan compared to last year. Subsequently, the number was reduced by the head of the Health Department to 1,624,070 yuan, a decrease of 32,510 yuan, or slightly less than 2%, compared to last year. A comparison of various expenses with last year shows slight increases in the "General" section of the General Affairs Department, the Pathology Laboratory, the Pharmacy, and the Cemetery, as well as the "Hospital" section of the Mental Hospital, the Chinese Isolation Hospital, the Tuberculosis Sanatorium, and the Nurses' Dormitory. There are fewer in the "General" section of the Chemical Laboratory, Cleaning, Milk, Markets, Food Inspection, and the "Hospital" section of the Management Department, the Isolation Hospital, and the Moganshan Sanatorium. In terms of personnel, only necessary minor changes have been included in this year's budget. In addition, there is 24,250 yuan under the inventory supplies item, totaling 1,648,320 yuan in recurrent expenditure, a decrease of 53,210 yuan compared to last year's 1,701,530 yuan.

Brother-in-law Steals Account Books: Wei Daosheng Surrenders Himself; Debate Concluded, Judgment Scheduled 138

Jinfa and Mianyuan, located on the second and third floors of No. 16 Yong'an Street, French Concession, specialize in import and export business. Suddenly, at midnight between 3 and 4 a.m. on January 14, someone sneaked in from the vacant house next door at No. 14 and stole all 33 account books belonging to Jinfa and Mianyuan. The victims reported the incident to the police for investigation. On the 27th of last month, Wei Daosheng, a bookkeeper at Jinfa (22 years old, from Fujian), surrendered to the police, claiming that he had stolen the account books and hid them in the Dafang Hotel and the Lequn Inn. Detective Hang Guangfu was dispatched and retrieved 24 account books from the two inns. There were still nine books missing. Wei was then sent to the Second Special Court, and the hearing was rescheduled. Yesterday morning, Judge Li Changnian questioned him again in the First Court. First, police lawyer Gu Shouxi stated the case and said that the defendant had committed the crimes of embezzlement and theft, and requested a trial. Then, Wu Zehong, manager of Jinfa, said that the defendant, Wei Daosheng, was the merchant's brother-in-law. He was recommended as an apprentice at the age of 15, and his conduct was usually very good. Therefore, he was promoted to the position of bookkeeper last year. He was very honest in the store, eating simple meals and wearing plain clothes. Therefore, the merchant trusted him very much. He did not know that he was secretly engaging in fraud. The defendant was afraid that he would be discovered when the accounts were settled at the end of the year, so he designed to steal the account books so that the merchant could not check the accounts. After the theft, the merchant did not suspect him at first. Later, when the silver in the account box suddenly went missing, he questioned him, but he only blushed and remained silent. Then, he left on a pretext and never returned, which aroused suspicion and led to a police investigation. It is now estimated that Wei embezzled more than 3,300 yuan. Sheng Jiepu, bookkeeper of Mianyuan, said that four of the merchant's stolen account books are still missing. Detective Hang Guangfu said that after the police received the plaintiff's report, detectives were dispatched to investigate. Later, according to reports, the defendant was often seen in Room 202 of the Kaitelin Apartment in Hongkou. When the police went to arrest him, Wei was gone, and only a few torn account books and a leather suitcase were found, containing brand new suits and leather shoes, which were purchased with the embezzled money. These clothes were worn to dance halls. On the 27th, the defendant surrendered to the police and confessed the location where the account books were hidden, so the police went to retrieve them. Wei Daosheng confessed to embezzlement and theft, but said that the money he obtained was used for bidding, speculation, and dance halls. He was deceived by others. According to the accountant's calculation, he only embezzled more than 1,000 yuan, not 3,300 yuan. Later, he felt guilty and surrendered to the police. Judge Li announced the conclusion of the debate and scheduled the judgment for the 11th.

Measures for the Transportation and Sale of Medical Supplies, Sulfur, etc.; Circular from the National New Pharmaceutical Industry Association 143

The National New Pharmaceutical Industry Federation yesterday sent a letter to the new pharmaceutical industry associations in various provinces and cities, stating that sulfur sublimate, potassium chlorate, potassium nitrate, and other items are widely used in medicine. Therefore, the first session of the Members' Representative Conference of the Federation resolved to submit a request to the competent authorities to formulate measures for the small-scale transportation and sale of medical supplies to facilitate business operations. Separate written requests have been submitted on file. Recently, the Jiangsu Provincial Salt and Sulfur Bureau issued Instruction No. 572 in the Su character of February 19th of this year, stating that the Ministry of Finance issued Instruction No. 2142 in the Salt character of December 30th of last year, forwarding the original document submitted by the association requesting the formulation of separate measures for the transportation and sale of sulfur and other items required for medical use. It is currently under review. In addition, the Ministry of Finance issued Instruction No. 22223 of January 31st of this year, approving the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's response to the same request from the association, ordering immediate investigation and reply for verification. Upon receiving this, it was determined that the nitrates and sulfur used in medicines were originally one of the supplies that should be within the scope of the transportation and sales department. However, if sulfur, potassium chlorate, and other items are used for medical purposes and are required to be of pure quality, which the transportation and sales department does not have, each drug dealer should still be allowed to file a record or apply for a passport as a special case for self-purchase and transportation. This has been handled for many years without any inconvenience. In the future, if the association needs to purchase and transport, it should first prepare documents according to the regulations, stating the annual quantity required by each drug dealer, and submit them to the bureau for verification. If the amount used by each drug dealer is within 200 catties, it can be handled as a special case and exempted from paying the remaining profits. It was reported to the Ministry of Finance, and Instruction No. 22569 in the Salt character of February 15th of this year stated, "Received the report. The proposed measures for the transportation of nitrates and sulfur for medical use are deemed feasible and should be approved. In addition to informing the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, please inform the National New Pharmaceutical Industry Association." In accordance with this, it is hereby notified to you.

Instructions from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce: Advertisement Record Books Should Be Stamped 144

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday sent a letter in reply to the Sino-Western Pharmacy, stating, "In reply to your letter of the 4th of this month, your company has a type of advertising record book and believes that it is purely for internal use and does not create external rights and obligations, and you inquired whether it should be stamped with a seal. According to Article 3, Item 8 of the Stamp Tax Law, 'internal use that does not create external rights and obligations' refers specifically to receipts and does not include books. According to Item 11 of the tax rate table, all general and branch books established for business purposes should be stamped, without any exception for internal use. Many merchants have misunderstood this point, and the Ministry of Finance has corrected them on record. This is for your information."

According to Dagong News Agency, the ink industry in this city is divided into two groups: "Sheji" and "Wuyuan". 工部局 Orchestra Concert Ticket Prices Remain the Same 155

The Shanghai Municipal Council Orchestra holds Sunday concerts every Sunday at the Lyceum Theatre. These concerts consist of classical symphony music and modern popular music alternately. Ticket prices for the former are divided into four categories: two yuan, one and a half yuan, one yuan, and sixty cents; the latter is divided into two categories: one yuan and a half yuan. Recently, there was a proposal to revise the ticket prices. However, according to the management of the concert, the current prices do not need to be changed. Based on the data since January 17th, the average number of listeners at symphony concerts was 546, with an average income of 596 yuan per concert. The average number of attendees at popular concerts was 685, with an average income of 422 yuan per concert. Therefore, based on the above attendance and income, there is no need to revise ticket prices this season.

Its entire inventory usually amounts to six to seven hundred thousand taels. It has always adhered to the principle of small profits and quick sales. The high quality of its goods and the sacrifice in pricing are well-known among Shanghai residents. In order to please customers and compete with fellow businesses, it has suffered significant losses and is ceasing operations for liquidation. Currently, it is urgently addressing debt repayment issues. The entire mortgaged inventory, through the mediation of prominent figures in Shanghai, will be publicly auctioned at 30% of its value. Due to the need to repay debts and the short time limit, and because the original location has already been leased, the Shanghai National Goods Company opposite the Hongmiao Temple on Nanjing Road has been temporarily borrowed as the auction location. It is heard that the entire inventory of the store still amounts to over 500,000 yuan, with most of it being valuable patterned silks and satins. There are also over 3,000 pieces of precious fine fur goods, all sold at 30% of their value. Other items include wool fabrics, new-style trimmings, and many patterns. The store is scheduled to hold a public auction starting on the 8th, which is sure to be a grand occasion.

National Physician Wang Weibai Relocates Clinic Wang Weibai, a national physician from Kunshan, is a third-generation family practitioner with twenty years of experience. He has a long-standing reputation in his hometown and has authored many books and accumulated rich experience. He has served as a standing committee member of the Kunshan branch of the National Medical and Pharmaceutical Association and the Chinese Medicine Association. Southwestern dignitaries Tang Shaochuan, Chen Shaozi, and Deng Zhiru welcomed him for consultations and presented him with inscriptions. He returned with acclaim. Soon after, he gained the appreciation of the master of Chinese studies, Zhang Taiyan, who advised him to practice medicine in Shanghai and set consultation rates on his behalf. In less than a year, recurrent illnesses arose. It is now heard that his original clinic on Guizhou Road was insufficient, and he has relocated to 20 Yuren Lane, Yunnan Road. He will be available for consultations at 2:00 PM on the second floor of the Xiang Sheng Motor General Office on Beijing Road. His future practice is expected to be prosperous.

The reason why the new legal tender can save the decline of Shanghai's real estate is mainly because the chips are looser than before, and real estate mortgages are easier to turn around; in addition, there are two points that have nothing to do with the new legal tender, but have a great impact on real estate. China's Women's Team Selected for International Basketball Competition; Dongya Defeats Zhenru Again Yesterday 165

The committee carefully reviewed the skills of each player in the pre-selection competition for this year's International Women's Basketball Team and selected the following twelve official representatives:

Liu Shouguang, Chen Rongtang, Xue Pixia, Chen Rongming, Ye Shunmei, Li Zhi, Chen Wanqing, Chen Jinchai, Xu Yuan, Yan Xiurong, Jiao Yulian, Guo Xinhua

The committee also resolved to hire Jiang Lianggui as the coach of the Chinese women's team and Chen Yude as the secretary.

The Dongya Women's Basketball Team played against Zhenru yesterday evening at Shenyuan as a pre-selection competition for the International Women's Basketball Team. The Dongya girls each showed their skills and defeated Zhenru with a score of 58 to 10.

In the first quarter, Liu Shouguang took the lead in scoring, and Xue Pi Huo and Chen Rongtang also contributed successively, with the score rising rapidly. Although Zhenru made repeated efforts, they failed to score, resulting in a score of 18 to 0.

In the second quarter, Zhenru tried to counterattack, and Ye Shunmei shot a ball after receiving passes from the left and right. After that, it was all the world of Dongya's Liu, Xue, and Chen, who moved freely. At halftime, the score was 37 to 2.

In the third quarter, Dongya had already gained a superior position. A group of female heroes was making fierce struggles. Zhenru's Ye and Chen scored successively.

In the fourth quarter, Zhenru actively attacked in an attempt to reverse the situation, while Dongya adopted a strategy of maintaining the status quo. The battle situation was similar to the previous quarter. When the time for competition was over, Dongya won a big victory with a score of 58 to 10. Provinces and Cities Send Personnel to Germany to Investigate Sports; Ten People in Total, with Each Person's Expenses Amounting to 2,000 Yuan, Borne by the Recommending Organization 166

(Nanjing, 5th Special Dispatch) The Ministry of Education approved the letter from the Chinese National Sports Promotion Association stating that in addition to sending representatives to this year's World Games, they requested to send sports personnel to Germany for investigation. The Ministry has formulated six regulations and notified all departments to handle and report them after considering the actual situation. The main points of the regulations: The members of the sports investigation team to Germany will be organized by the education departments of each province and city by selecting personnel who meet the following conditions: A. Graduates of domestic and foreign universities or sports colleges who have served in the sports field for more than two years and are still continuing to serve. B. Those who have the above qualifications and are proficient in one of the English, French, and German languages. C. Those who are over 25 years old and under 40 years old, healthy in body and mind, with no trachoma and no bad habits. Qualified personnel should submit detailed resumes to the Ministry for verification before the end of April. Before going abroad, all qualified personnel should report to the Ministry, and the Ministry will convene a meeting to decide on the group's investigation matters. The expenses shall be raised by the recommending organization itself, with 2,000 yuan per person, including 1,000 yuan for travel expenses, 600 yuan for food and accommodation expenses, and 200 yuan each for clothing and miscellaneous expenses. The total number of members shall be limited to ten. The period of going abroad shall be from June to September.

Western Youth Volleyball Dispute; Central Youth Team Decides to Withdraw 169

The volleyball team organized by the members of the Central Youth Association has participated in the Western Youth Volleyball League in previous years, winning every game and repeatedly winning championships. All the team members are national players or athletes of the Games, so their skills are unparalleled. Unfortunately, this year, they repeated their participation in the Western Youth League. Because most of the team members usually pay attention to basketball, they lack practice in volleyball and have unfamiliar cooperation. Since the start of the Western Youth League, they have lost to the Russian army in the first game and were defeated by Haiqing in the second game. When the team played against Haiqing, the referee, Plata, made unfair judgments and reversed his decisions, which was considered unsatisfactory. At that time, they obeyed the rules of the referee and did not argue. However, the next day, they sent a written letter to the Chairman of the Sports Committee of the Western Youth to protest. Unexpectedly, there was no satisfactory answer, but only perfunctory excuses. Therefore, in the game against Haiqing on the 2nd of this month, they painfully gave up the game, and the Western Youth still showed no response. Therefore, the members of the Central Youth team became more indignant and believed that they could not continue to cooperate, so they decided to withdraw from this year's volleyball tournament.

National Children

On the 4th, the Ministry of Education issued a circular to the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities, stating: "According to the report from the National Children's Year Implementation Committee, this committee, in order to promote children's painting and inspire their artistic interest, has decided to hold a National Children's Painting Exhibition in Shanghai in August of this year. In accordance with the committee's outline, the solicitation of exhibits should be requested by this committee to order your ministry to instruct subordinate primary schools in all provinces and cities to select works. Detailed rules for soliciting works have been formulated. A copy of the 'Detailed Rules for Soliciting Works for the Children's Painting Exhibition' is enclosed for your ministry's review. It is requested that you instruct the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities to instruct all public and private primary schools and kindergartens to select and submit works as scheduled in accordance with the regulations and methods, and submit them to the competent educational administrative organs of their respective provinces, cities, and districts for sorting, examination, and creation of a list, and then send them to the Shanghai National Children's Painting Exhibition for display and exhibition. This is for public convenience, etc." Based on this, we are issuing a copy of the "Detailed Rules for Soliciting Works for the National Children's Painting Exhibition" to instruct subordinate public and private primary schools and kindergartens to select and submit works as scheduled in accordance with the current regulations, which will be sorted by the department, a list created, and sent to the Shanghai National Children's Painting Exhibition. Please comply accordingly. This order.

Key Points for Soliciting Exhibits for the National Children's Painting Exhibition

Purpose: The main purpose of the National Children's Painting Exhibition is twofold: A. To inspire children's artistic interest, cultivate aesthetic instincts, and unleash creative nature. B. To study children's artistic tendencies, test imaginative abilities, and assist in improving brotherly children's art education.

Principles: Based on the above purpose, this painting exhibition is purely for testing and research purposes and has no meaning in terms of achievement assessment or competition. The quality of the exhibits has no relationship to the honor or disgrace of children, teachers, or parents. Therefore, the selection of exhibits should fully consider children's creative abilities. Works that have been participated in or modified by teachers or parents will not be accepted. The committee will pay the utmost attention and importance to the standards of acceptance and rejection of exhibits. It is hoped that all primary schools and children's parents across the country will thoroughly understand and assist in the above purpose and principles.

Investigation: In order to further study children's artistic interests and abilities, the committee will conduct the following supplementary investigations: A. Children's place of production (details of their village). B. Children's special interests. C. Parents' names, ages, occupations, and their special interests. D. The names, ages, genders, resumes, and interests in art education of the school's drawing and painting teachers. It is hoped that teachers in all primary schools will send a detailed list with the selected exhibits, which will be sent to the education bureaus of each province and city for forwarding to the committee for joint research.

Detailed Rules for Soliciting Exhibits for the National Children's Painting Exhibition (Approved at the Second Preparatory Meeting on January 27, 25th Year)

Article 1: The National Children's Painting Exhibition (hereinafter referred to as the "Committee") aims to study and promote children's painting, inspire children's creativity, and improve art education.

Article 2: The Committee is scheduled to be held in Shanghai from June 6th for a period of ten days.

Article 3: All public and private registered primary schools and kindergartens nationwide must select and submit exhibits for display and exhibition in accordance with these detailed rules.

Article 4: All exhibits participating in the Committee shall be free drawings by children (covering sketches, impressions, color, and monochrome).

Article 5: There are no specified sizes or types of paper for the paintings, and no mounting is required.

Article 6: The solicitation of exhibits shall be submitted by the National Children's Year Implementation Committee to the Ministry of Education to instruct the educational administrative organs of all provinces, cities, and districts to instruct their subordinate primary schools and kindergartens to select five creative works from each child, which shall be collected and reviewed by the educational administrative organs of each province, city, and district and submitted to the Preparatory Committee by May 10th along with a list of exhibits.

Article 7: The items in the exhibit list are as follows: 1. Number (numbered by each province, city, and district as the numbering unit, determined by the educational administrative organs of each province, city, and district). 2. Painting title. 3. Exhibiting school. 4. Author's name. 5. Remarks.

Article 8: The items required on the exhibit label are as follows: 1. Number (numbered by this committee). 2. Painting title. 3. Exhibiting school. 4. Author's name. 5. Gender. 6. Actual age. 7. Native place. 8. Grade. 9. Production date. 10. Remarks.

Article 9: The above exhibits will be reviewed by this committee after they are received and displayed. The review criteria will be determined separately.

Article 10: This committee will hire children's painting experts to form an evaluation committee to jointly evaluate and provide opinions, classifying them into different grades. The selected works will be presented by the National Children's Year Implementation Committee to the Ministry of Education for commendation and appropriate awards.

Article 11: If it is discovered that any exhibit was not created by the child himself and the facts are verified, the National Children's Year Implementation Committee will request the Ministry of Education to punish the responsible teachers and staff.

Article 12: All exhibits of this committee will not be returned, but may be transported to various provinces, cities, and districts for exhibition. The method will be determined separately.

Article 13: The Preparatory Committee of this committee is located in the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau in the central district of Shanghai.

Article 14: If there are any deficiencies in these detailed rules, they may be revised by this committee at any time.

Measures for Expanding the Celebration of Children's Day 176

The National Children's Year Implementation Committee has scheduled to hold the tenth general meeting of the Educational Technology Section at 10:00 AM on the 7th of this month (Saturday) to discuss matters related to the exhibition of children's educational tools and toys, and to report on the conclusion of the children's reading exhibition. The outline of the measures for expanding the celebration of Children's Day, as determined by the committee, is recorded below:

1. The local Children's Year Implementation Committees should, in conjunction with the local Party Headquarters, convene representatives of relevant agencies three weeks before Children's Day (April 4th) to organize the "Preparatory Committee for Expanding the Celebration of Children's Day," responsible for designing and organizing all matters related to the expanded celebration of Children's Day.

2. The National Children's Year Implementation Committee should report on the news of National Children's Day on the Central Broadcasting Station on this day, broadcast Children's Year songs, and invite the Chairman of the National Government and the President of the Executive Yuan to speak to the people of the country.

3. Local preparatory committees should send letters to the local police authorities, notifying all agencies and shops to hang the Party and national flags on Children's Day to extend the celebration.

4. On Children's Day, celebration ceremonies should be held, and art performances, speech contests, children's sports meets, children's achievement exhibitions, lantern festivals, etc. should be held as much as possible to extend the celebration, but the principle should be simple, easy to implement, and not cause children to feel hardship.

5. On Children's Day, bookstores should issue commemorative booklets for Children's Day and give them to children, and newspapers should publish special issues for children to promote the event.

6. Local preparatory committees should send letters to the local Party Headquarters and administrative agencies to send personnel on Children's Day to inspect relevant children's welfare agencies and groups and provide guidance, promotion, or improvement as needed.

7. Localities should elect a number of children's representatives to visit the heads of local governments to express their sincerity in trusting the government.

8. Local preparatory committees should send letters to local entertainment venues to perform various programs related to children's education on Children's Day, and give special preferential treatment to children by not selling tickets or reducing ticket prices appropriately.

9. Local preparatory committees should send letters to local shops selling children's items to offer special discounts on Children's Day to commemorate the event.

10. Local preparatory committees should produce commemorative badges for Children's Day (Children's Year) and distribute them to local children for permanent commemoration.

11. Local preparatory committees should prepare stationery and food, etc. to be distributed to children.

12. Various gatherings held in various places should allow children to participate enthusiastically and give them special preferential treatment.

13. Local preparatory committees with radio stations or broadcasting stations should make full use of the stations to broadcast lectures on children's issues and include children's programs.

14. Local preparatory committees with aircraft stationed should send letters to aviation agencies to send aircraft to perform aerial demonstrations in the sky on this day and distribute small slogans.

15. Local preparatory committees (Preparatory Committee for Expanding the Celebration of Children's Day) should, in addition to designating school scouts to serve at various gathering places, send letters to the local military, police, and constabulary to maintain order.

16. Local preparatory committees may add other celebration items as appropriate according to local conditions.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Boy (1) (9) (1) 178

— Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"Those bears?" Robert asked with interest.

"No, it refers to those 'Pilgrims' because the Indians often made things difficult for them. They didn't have enough food to eat, and they had to carry guns on the way to church. Many people died. Later, they simply moved from the ship and landed on a large stone called 'Plymouth Rock' (Note 4), which Aunt Shu also saw and touched. These people later subdued the Indians and gradually became rich. They are all very good; one of my distant ancestors also came from those ships. One of the ships was called Mayflower (Note 5). They created Thanksgiving, which we have often had since, and I love this festival very much. Please give me some more turkey."

"I think Xiao Qiao will become a historian in the future. He narrates those facts so clearly," Uncle Fulizi's eyes turned towards Aunt Shu, filled with smiles. At the same time, he gave some more turkey to the descendants of those early settlers.

"I thought a person could eat as much as they wanted on Thanksgiving. But Fulang just said that you shouldn't eat too much even at this time," said Tai Fei with a somewhat uneasy look on his face, probably because he had received some warning.

"Fulang is right, so be careful with your knife again. Don't eat too much, otherwise, you won't be able to join in doing that unexpected thing later," said Mrs. Shu.

(Note 4) Plymouth Rock (Note 5) Mayflower

The Fourth Term of the Municipal Literacy School in This City Has Already Started 182

In order to eliminate illiteracy and popularize education in this city, the municipal government has been implementing compulsory literacy education since July 1st of last year, organizing literacy schools. Three terms have already graduated. The fourth term of literacy schools, consisting of 210 schools, has been prepared and has started classes in various districts. This term will end at the end of May this year. It is heard that due to funding issues, the municipal government is still considering whether to continue organizing after the end of this term.

As a result, it is rumored that Japanese trading companies such as Mitsui and Yoshida will establish factories in Shanghai to weave woolen fabrics, hoping to defeat Yihua's products. According to detailed investigations by reporters, Japanese trading companies do have this plan, and sooner or later they will establish factories in Shanghai for weaving.

Yuanfang Piece Goods Sales Are Sluggish 199

Yesterday, Thursday was the date for Yuanfang to call at the village. 50 boxes of various goods were arranged. Due to the cold weather and sluggish sales, the price of goods fell further. Taixi satin prices were still stable, one yuan velvet had no rise or fall, Yuanzhi wool and Yuanfu silk fluctuated slightly, and feather silk piece prices fell by several jiao to one yuan. However, the Shangshan map only fell by 0.2 yuan, and red and blue foreign cloth were sold at a fixed weekly price. Foreign yarn also fell, and the cloth sold in season as the weather was cold.

Shen Bao Literary and Art Weekly

Mason 200

— Ouyang Shan

Three miles from the city, a small path along the fields led into the countryside. There were no cars or horses, only farmers walking back and forth barefoot, carrying their vegetables, small bundles of firewood, and hay on their shoulders, sometimes with their small children. With cigarettes in their mouths, they displayed an air of peace, strength, and an inscrutable cunning. "Canada Dyeing and Cleaning Factory"—this was a flamboyant name. Surrounded by bamboo fences in front of us, a black painted sign with these words in white oil paint. Opposite, there was a low hill covered with various styles of tombs.

Standing in the shallow, clear creek, about twenty of us were working about twenty or thirty feet west of the path. Mason's position was closest to me on the left. We took the boiled clothes out of the soda pot, lightly dipped them in water, and swung them into the air, forcefully hitting them on the stone slab... repeating this process, then pressing down with our full body weight to wring out the dirt. The foam splashed into the stream, turning it milky white and muddy.

We hadn't even finished smoking a cigarette when the company's food delivery truck honked its horn on the highway far to the east—it had become a habit. But that day, because the regular driver's wife was sick and a novice was filling in, we were exceptionally granted a very pleasant fifteen-minute break.

Mason and I found a clean grave site on the opposite low hill, and we lay on the gray sandy ground, stretching our bodies as much as possible. The gray sand was warm, like a hard baking sheet on a stove, and the winter sun covered us with a soft, comfortable warmth.

"This sky... is the same one above our heads every day. Do you believe it?"

He started by looking incredulous. "Do you often pay attention to it?" Having said that, he opened his eyes in surprise.

And then he slowly added, "It's very cold to me."

Our surroundings were quiet and beautiful. A gentle breeze swayed through the new pine forest, rustling gently back and forth above us. The yellow weeds stubbornly crawled on the ground, as if they were fully drawn springs, exerting all their strength to resist the insidious suction of the soil. ... Not a single bird was seen. Only army ants, small beetles, and grasshoppers quietly busied themselves on the dry hillside. ...

The sky was filled with bright colors that one wouldn't expect in winter—light purple and light blue, like a wild lake that hasn't been trampled by vulgar, frivolous, and self-important tourists, with fragments of lotus flowers floating on it. Its orange-red, huge single eye—a huge, incomparably large, cannon-like eye—flashed with golden light.

Two parallel cloud rifts cut straight across half the sky, inserting themselves into the sun's halo, just like vehicle tracks. I felt that the tomb we were lying on had begun to shake and was traveling swiftly along those tracks. Mason nudged my ribs with his elbow.

"I say our shop has become a company of the vanquished."

The way he said that made me happy. "Company of the vanquished" was a flavorful term created by the people of Guangzhou more than a decade ago. At that time, three major companies had been cursed for exclusively selling inferior goods. ... I knew that Mason's judgment referred to our "Canada" company accepting a batch of dyes. This batch of dyes was shipped in by a merchant from Shanghai named Wu Lifu, who called his goods "sacrifices."

I didn't answer him. I asked him something else.

"...Later, what else did that Shanghainese say, that egg sac!—Every time he comes to the provincial capital, he curses the people he meets in Shanghai; last time it was his uncle, the time before that, it was his mistress..."

"If you listen to him, the students in Shanghai are wrong," Mason pointed out to me. "They declare that only they are qualified to be patriotic, and no one else is allowed. ... Wu Lifu enthusiastically described how frivolous, arrogant, and dismissive those students were of other people's patriotic actions... He said that once, a blacksmith shouted loudly at a large group of students, and the young people actually attacked him, beating him half to death. ... In Shanghai, everyone laughs when you mention the students..."

"They're not as smart as we are here. 'Staff and Workers'—we're right. ..."

"It's not worth letting that Shanghainese chew on it."

"That's right. But damn it, — does he even know what's right and wrong..."

We fell silent. Mason was depressed. One of his arms was bent on the ground, pressing down on his own hand.

The sky underwent an even more beautiful transformation. The cloud rifts split into more streaks, the tracks disappeared—that one-eyed, enormous head was covered with strands of hair, hanging all the way to the edge of the sky. Crimson fragments merged into large blocks of various shapes, as if they were about to sink down.

"Are you worried about that Shanghainese?"

"Shanghainese, no. When I want to do something, I don't care about anyone," Mason said. "I'm unhappy because of my mother-in-law. ... She forces me because of money... She deceives me because of money... She mocks me because of money. I beat her hard this morning. ..."

Mason and I later burst out laughing.

We needed to laugh. We needed this brief and precious rest—for our endless work, hardship, poverty, and the inescapable depression that only eroded our strength.

This is Also a Human 201

Zola's Writing Method 202

— Chen Hannian

In the late nineteenth century, the writing method of naturalistic novels, through the hands of Balzac, and then Flaubert, and finally Zola, reached its perfection.

Zola said that he himself could not create a plot. He believed that a person is a product of environment and heredity, so he always started writing novels by researching these two aspects. He once said to a friend:

"When I start writing a novel, I am not troubled by the plot. I have no idea where to insert the story, which characters will appear in which places, or how the story will begin and end."

In order to research a character, he always collects all kinds of documents that can help him. He has three research paths: first, historical books; second, written or oral evidence; and finally, he personally goes to the scene of the incident to observe.

He said: "Every time I write a novel, I am always surrounded by books on the subject; I always find many experts to talk to me; I also have to travel myself to see the place, the people, and the morality of the place."

He takes notes during his travels. He records the appearance of the characters, the scenery, and fragments of conversations.

He then classifies and organizes the documents he has collected, binds them into volumes, and puts them in beautiful book covers. He calls this first step "the organization of book covers."

We can see that Zola is like a respectable and erudite scholar in the first step of his work. He has been immersed in research, collecting materials, but now he is going to move on to the second stage: the stage of imagination.

He now begins to sketch. He thinks where he goes, and writes where he goes, without talking about art or rhetoric. In this way, he writes the outline of the novel. He then revises the outline again and again, making it specific from the general. In terms of characters, he first divides them into classes, and then pulls out the individual from the class. After such step-by-step sketching, a series of events naturally emerge around these characters.

After he has a full understanding of the plot, he begins to deal with the characters. He records all the past behaviors of the character: career, age, health, physique, temperament, habits, social relations, etc., without missing anything, like a judge interrogating a criminal. In this way, the behavior of the protagonist in his novel is determined.

At this time, his book covers gradually swell, and his work requires more precise selection. Sometimes, the novel he writes is only two volumes, but the book covers containing the materials of the novel are three or four times larger than the novel.

Once the materials are collected, he starts to deal with the structure of the whole book chapter by chapter. He himself said: "I work step by step, I embellish my sketches, and put all the important facts in the appropriate place. The same is true for the placement of characters: here is a description of the physical form, there is a description of the prominent personality; further, the psychological state of the protagonist that I want to suggest is selected. I overturn each book cover, and everything necessary is placed in its proper place; the scene of the incident, the houses, the scenery... must all be distributed and interspersed harmoniously according to the plot of the story. Now I have already outlined the rough lines of the structure. But this is still rough. The events contained in each chapter are randomly inserted when I pour out my book covers. Therefore, before I start real writing, I have to determine a "fixed plan" from the "original" plan and the pile of materials, separating and linking them chapter by chapter, completely following the sequence of the action's progress. At this time, it is just like before a drama is staged, all the materials for the performance are prepared."

This is the time to open the curtain. This is the most pleasant part of his work, and it is also the final step in his writing: carefully polishing and transcribing.

He quietly and regularly revises and transcribes. He writes four manuscript pages a day, neatly and almost without any corrections. After writing, he puts them aside and never looks at them again before publishing. Yes, he doesn't need to look at them again. In the long hours of work, he has revised and considered countless times, and he can be so firmly confident.

Talking About New Year Pictures 203

— Li Xuan

The New Year pictures in the old customs, the New Year pictures I want to talk about now, are the New Year pictures of Hebei Province under that special environment. In the past, the New Year pictures of Hebei Province could probably be divided into three categories.

The first is stone prints on pink paper or woodblock prints, with bright red and green colors, and very heavy color matching. Most of them are printed very badly. The black line outline is first printed on the paper, and then when reprinting various colors, they often do not match the outline. Therefore, when a character or other thing is published in this picture, it becomes a blurred shadow that is twisted to the east and skewed to the west. This is a handicraft. There is also a kind of printing that is more refined than the kind mentioned above. It is printed on newsprint by machine. The size of these two kinds is the same (two and a half feet wide and one foot high, rectangular). The content is also taken from a martial arts, funny, loyal, filial, chaste, or obscene old opera, or several fat children, as well as auspicious paintings that are warmly welcomed by farmers, such as the Heavenly Official Giving Blessings and Treasure Horses Carrying Gold.

Second: These are horizontal banners that are twice as large as the previous two. They were not very popular at first. The themes are all fragments of old novels, a folk tale, or stories of agricultural harvest, etc. After the September 18th Incident, another kind of painting appeared. For example, the Volunteer Army jumped up to resist the enemy, occupied "Shenyang City", and "Bombed Jinzhou", etc. By the end of 1933, there were even more farcical scenes of puppets taking the stage, Ma Zhanshan's snowy night march, and the heroic Shanghai Battle of the 19th Route Army, the magnificent posture of the civilian volunteer big sword teams, and the wounded soldier hospitals and ambulances in the rear. In the north, there were New Year pictures of the 29th Army's bloody defense of Xifengkou, Sun Dianying's deep penetration of the isolated army, and the loss of the world's first pass. ... The materials taken by the authors of these paintings were mostly reproductions or derivations of wartime photographs and news articles from newspapers and books in major ports.

In terms of consciousness, some parts contain patriotic ideas, and other parts can be said to be faithful reports. In terms of expression techniques, they all inherit the old forms of the past, so they can only reveal things to the farmers in an unsophisticated way, but cannot move their emotions.

Third, are exquisite and realistic small four-frame books, mostly scenery, serial pictures of old novels with broken waists and truncated backs, or longer legends, as well as depictions of elegant small decorations such as piano, chess, calligraphy, painting, pine, bamboo, and plum. In addition, there is a kind of vertical or horizontal large rectangle, with extremely exquisite painting, color, and paper materials. The things printed on it are god statues, beauties, famous horses, Chinese movie stars, opera costumes, and barefooted girls with disheveled hair. Therefore, this painting also brings new influences. The young men and women in the families of the wealthy in general towns and towns are doing their best to imitate the clothes and costumes of the people in the paintings, so the current clothes of the local young masters and young ladies are somewhat nondescript and semi-urbanized—the patrons of this valuable painting are all landlords, merchants, agency staff, and the families of petty officials.

The first category is that the masses are anesthetized by evil thoughts for many years. Although they are currently in extreme poverty, they have to place their fantasies on auspicious paintings, or inherit the transmitted anesthetic power to "appreciate" the only toxic painting. Because in terms of purchasing power, this kind of painting is also the most suitable.

The third category is for people who have nowhere to use their energy all year round. The older generation knows that they have done a lot of evil, so they buy a statue of a god to worship, repair their afterlife, or talk about things that are not as good as the past while looking at the paintings and feeling sentimental, and take the opportunity to play with some refreshing elegance. The younger generation loves the novelty of different places, bold eroticism, and wants to know more about the enjoyment of the owners of other places.

What we need to pay attention to here is the second category. It is a commercial venture with merchants starting from the point of seeking profit, and although the content contains many components that speak for themselves, it can partially reflect reality, and the effect of painting in poor remote areas that the power of newspapers cannot reach. It does have a wide range of groups, although it is sometimes toxic. However, in the absence of another better mass art to take on this task now, this kind of New Year picture has its own significance.

Artists of the new era, please do not neglect this department of art. (End)

Being Obscured by What's in Front of Your Eyes Allows Blindness to Deceive 204

— Zikai Painting

The Life of Romain Rolland 205

— Yongni

This year is the seventieth birthday of Romain Rolland. The seventy-year life of this great representative of European culture marks the milestones in the progress of world culture. To explore the path of his ideological development, it is necessary to relive the biography of this historical giant.

Romain Rolland was born in 1866 in a small market town in central France to a modest family. His father was a notary, and his mother was a staunch Catholic believer. Romain Rolland's childhood, according to Jean Bonnerot, the author of "The Biography of Romain Rolland," was probably like Olivier in "Jean-Christophe," a blond, thin, not very tall child. He inherited the temperament of a revolutionary from his revolutionary great-grandfather. When he was still a child, the memory of the Commune in 1871 penetrated deeply into his small brain. He was raised in the tradition of the French Revolution and the Enlightenment. His faith and his love of music were influenced by his mother.

Shortly after the Franco-Prussian War, he began to study at the local school. His parents originally hoped that he would study mathematics and physics in the future, but Rolland, who had a strong need for fantasy, legends, and beliefs, did not like mathematical sciences. He loved music so much that it seemed that without music, there would be no fun. This unparalleled love for music can be said to be a major feature of the young Rolland's personality. In addition to the music of Beethoven, Schubert, Wagner, etc., what he loved was Shakespeare's plays.

Because of his enthusiasm for classical music and Shakespeare, Rolland failed the teacher's college entrance examination twice, and only managed to pass it on the third try. He initially intended to study literature, but only began to study history and geography in his second year. This had a great influence on his life as an artist, because studying history and geography, and taking a broad view of the past and present, not only expanded his horizons, making him a supranationalist later on, but also provided his various works, especially his masterpiece "Jean-Christophe," with great ideas and rich materials.

From his childhood in the countryside, Rolland loved great people, heroes, and artists of the world. However, his love was different from the ordinary young man's worship of heroes, but only a longing for heroes with a deep love for God and man. He was obsessed with Prometheus, who resisted Zeus and stole fire for mankind, and admired and admired Tolstoy, an idealist who appeared in the European literary world at that time as an apostle of the only God. As an unknown French youth, he boldly wrote to this great Russian writer, asking him for guidance on how to live and how to create. Tolstoy sensed great sincerity in this letter and, exceptionally, wrote back to this young man. This was a long letter of thirty-eight pages, all written in French. "Dear friend," the letter began, "I received your first letter. It touched my heart. I read it with tears." Regarding art, he also wrote down his opinions. "Only art that unites people is the only valuable art. A valuable artist does not hesitate to sacrifice for his beliefs. The first prerequisite for all real occupations is not the love of art, but the love of mankind. Only those who are filled with such love are suitable for doing what an artist is worth doing." From then on, Rolland became a loyal disciple of Tolstoy, and the sound of Tolstoy's righteousness resounded loudly in his art.

After graduating from the Normal School with honors, Rolland was sent by the school to study in Rome. In Rome, he saw the beautiful Italian scenery and the brilliant ancient art. The Shakespearean plays he saw there revived his dreams of the past. He intended to learn from Shakespeare how he portrayed England in historical dramas, and to write about the Renaissance era in dramas. One day, while walking on the Janiculum, one of the seven hills of Rome, he decided to write a work with the whole of Europe as the stage. This was the beginning of his later masterpiece "Jean-Christophe." He met the German revolutionary Malwida von Meysenbug in Rome. This old woman, who lived a tragic, sad, and ridiculed life, but always maintained a quiet, clear, and young soul, can be said to be Rolland's second mother. He wrote "Jean-Christophe" partly under her inspiration and suggestion.

After passing the thesis entitled "The Origin of Modern Lyrical Drama," he became a lecturer in music at the Normal School in Paris. He launched a "People's Theater" movement to oppose the bourgeois dramas of the metropolis, and wrote three revolutionary plays: "July 14," "Danton," and "Wolves." He sang the praises of popular art (art and theater for the people and by the people). From 1900 to 1903, he wrote many drama essays, which were later collected in the book "People's Theater."

In 1904, he wrote "The Life of Michelangelo," and later wrote "The Life of Tolstoy," which together with his early "The Life of Beethoven" formed a series of "Heroic Biographies."

In 1904, he began to write his novel "Jean-Christophe." This was his lifelong work. In it, the author made a profound and merciless analysis of the evils of capitalism, completely exposing the mask of decadent bourgeois culture, and portrayed a typical intellectual with a strong personality and heroic aspirations.

Romain Rolland, who was once known in Paris as a music specialist and playwright, although he wrote outstanding biographies and dramas, and completed the great "Jean-Christophe," and was already forty years old, had not yet received fame and monetary rewards. The "tragedy of French idealism" he spoke of had been personally experienced. It was not until 1914, when he was almost fifty years old, that the world recognized the existence of Romain Rolland as a great artist and idealist. The French Academy of Literature awarded a prize to the ten volumes of "Jean-Christophe," and at the same time, the world's Nobel Prize was awarded to the author of this great work.

1914 was not a happy year for Rolland. The World War broke out in September of that year. This was a very painful blow to Rolland. He left his motherland and fled to Switzerland, publishing his famous anti-war essay "Above the Battle" in Joutnal de Geneve, waging a bloodless war against war with the weapons of pacifism.

The crisis of post-war capitalism from 1919 to 1920 made many progressive writers gradually sympathize with the revolution, and the "Clarté" group, which combined all thinkers and artists who sympathized with the revolution, was formed, and Rolland was a famous member of this group. As he himself admitted in the preface to his collection of essays "Fifteen Years of Combat," the five years from 1920 to 1927 were a period of hesitation and groping for him, and he did not say goodbye to his petty-bourgeois past and join the new team until later. The famous "Farewell to the Past" is an important document in which Rolland clearly expressed his new creed.

This ideological transformation was reflected in his "The Enchanted Soul," published in 1933. The first volume, written from 1923 to 1926, bears clear traces of the author's hesitation, but the final part reflects the author's new world view.

Continuous literary activities did not prevent Rolland from actively participating in the social liberation movement. His practical activities against imperialism and war are well known to the world. And this, like Barbusse, who died not long ago, and Gorky, who is still alive, is precisely where Rolland is greatest.

A Night of Injury 206

— Mei Zhi

Junior middle school was over, but I couldn't find a job despite exhausting all my efforts. With the adventurous mentality of "recovering capital" from a gambling den, my father borrowed one hundred dollars by hook or by crook. I myself crammed day and night to review those subjects, and finally passed the silkworm breeding school, which was said to earn fifty or sixty dollars a month after graduation.

Less than half a month after entering, it was time to raise silkworms. The five rooms we used to call classrooms are now filled with round bamboo trays. The tiny black ant-like things placed in the trays require the energy of more than twenty poor girls to care for. The first sleep stage is over, and now it is the time when they eat the most leaves. More than twenty of us often can't sleep well for most of the night.

After being woken up by my roommate, I knew it was almost time to go to work. Drowsily putting on my clothes, I touched the classroom by the light of the stars in the sky. My head was stinging slightly, and my eyes seemed to be covered with a thin film. I only saw piles of grayish-white wriggling animals in the round trays and green mulberry leaves, but my eyes could hardly see them. I hurriedly grabbed the mulberry leaves, chopped them finely with a knife, and mechanically sent them handful by handful into the trays. Running back and forth like this, my legs were so weak that I just wanted to lie on the floor. My eyelids also wanted to close tightly. There were still more than a dozen trays of leaves that had not been added, and I could not rest. I was cutting the leaves without any feeling, my eyes often closing unconsciously, dozing off with a shudder, but the iron-faced image of the dorm supervisor was always waving before my eyes. I don't know how long it went on like this, when suddenly there was a "whoosh" sound, and a cold and thorny sensation drilled straight into my heart. This shock made me open my eyes wide. Looking down, I saw steaming blood gushing out from my ring finger and middle finger. Fresh, steaming blood was flowing on the mulberry leaves and the cutting board. I didn't feel any pain, but my hand seemed to be paralyzed. I didn't feel scared, and I didn't even think about how to stop the bleeding, but just held these two fingers with my left hand. The blood continued to drip onto the floor like two drops, and the blood on the floor quickly formed a red sun, one point at a time. This color emitted a glittering brilliance, and the surrounding darkness was suffocating me. The lamplight, as big as the tears of a resentful woman, was emitting a color like the face of a dying person. This color, like the face of an anemic person, immediately made me think: blood is flowing from my own body right now! This color, this color! Oh my! Why has my face turned like this! The whole house was filled with the faces of dying people, the faces of anemic people! This is Ying! This is skinny Li's face, and that is the crying Fang. Oh no! What happened to you all… I shouted as if I was possessed.

This sound startled Wang in the next room, and the first thing she saw when she ran in was the blood on the floor. She panicked and didn't know what to do. She stood by the door for a while and ran away. After a while, she woke up our dorm supervisor, a widowed old woman in her fifties. This tigress kept scolding all the way, "Making a fuss in the middle of the night…" But when she came in and saw me, a Zen master who had lost too much blood, she was a little flustered too. She looked at my hand, but turned around and told Wang to go to her room to get the water pipe. The water pipe! When someone is in danger, is she thinking about smoking?…

But Wang had no choice but to get it for her. The tigress opened the tobacco pouch, grabbed a handful of tobacco, and aimed it at my bleeding wound. Press. Oh my! Heavens! This was even more painful than a sharp knife piercing my heart. My eyes seemed to be sparking, my hands jumping up like fleas, my heart jumping up too, my face burning like a drunkard's. I endured the tears and listened to this mother's lecture. Raising a hand that was burning with pain, I was helped back to my bed by Wang. I was seized by anger, sadness, and pain. I thought of my father's frustrated face after how many bows he had to make to borrow a sum of money from fat Zhu at four percent interest, I thought of the hardships this old woman had put me through since entering the school, and I thought of the graduates who often came back to negotiate with the old woman but got no results... Graduation! Finding a job! Supporting a family! Holding this painful hand, I cried myself to sleep on the bed.

Siam Opposes the "New Press Law" 207

— Jian Ping

After Venezuela's victory in opposing press censorship, we see that the people's representatives of Siam are also opposing the "New Press Law," which is similar to press censorship regulations. According to a telegram from Bangkok, the capital of Siam, published on February 29th: In the extraordinary session of the Siamese parliament, the people's representatives proposed a case of "opposing the New Press Law." The main reason stated: "The government must grant the press the highest right to freedom of speech. If the government has no fault, why fear attacks in words?" As a result, it has been passed in the meeting, acknowledging the reason in principle, and is now being reviewed by nine people. It is found that this case is sympathetic to the damage done to the speech, assembly, association, and education of overseas Chinese in Thailand.

The demand for freedom of speech can be said to be a common feeling of people all over the world. It is not only to fight for the rights that people should enjoy, but also a sharp weapon for the entire country and the entire nation to fight for independence and survival. We should all express sympathy for Venezuela's opposition to press censorship regulations and the proposal of the people's representatives of Siam to oppose the "New Press Law."

As for Siam, a country, a primary school teacher who had lived there for a long time and is still being unreasonably oppressed once told me. Although Siam is nominally an independent constitutional monarchy, most of the power is in the hands of the British. Recently, because a certain imperialist obtained part of the power in that place, the policy of fooling the people followed the economic invasion, and the result was the promulgation of the "New Press Law" and the closure or unreasonable expulsion of schools run by overseas Chinese. Not long ago, I believe everyone will not forget the tension of the anti-Chinese atmosphere in Siam. Now, their people are aware and dare to propose opposition to the "New Press Law," which is the second point that we have to admire. At the same time, we can see that only the weak truly sympathize with the weak. The people of Siam do not exclude the Chinese. Anti-Chinese sentiment is just a means of imperialism.

Now, let's go back to whether the opposition to the "New Press Law" is reasonable? Of course, it is undeniably reasonable, as long as the government is still the people's government. As the representative put forward the reason: "If the government has no fault, why fear attacks in words?" True speech is not an attack on the government, but a contribution of opinions and a correction of those faults. It is about the "matter," not the "government." For example, not long ago, the people of Britain and France opposed the "Italian-Abyssinian Peace Agreement," opposing the government's failure to sacrifice weak nations and giving convenience to aggressors, not opposing the government. This is very obvious. From this, we can understand the reason why "the government must give the press the highest right to freedom of speech." At the same time, speech is also a sharp weapon of national defense, much like the current international news agencies, such as the French Havas Agency, the British Reuters Agency, the Japanese Denstu Agency, the Allied News Agency, the Soviet TASS, etc., which one does not speak for their own country.

In addition to hoping that the Siamese government will realize and return freedom to the people, we also hope that all countries with similar unreasonable laws on press censorship will also automatically abolish them.

Nora (6) 208

— Wan Chao-chen, Xin Xin cooperation

Nora was telling Helmer how to handle the housework after she left. The doorbell in the outer hall rang, and the maid Ellen came in and said, "A lady visitor wants to see you, Madam."

Helmer instructed her not to see the visitor, and then went to the study. Ellen led Mrs. Linden in.

Mrs. Linden: (Hesitatingly, with doubt) Nora, how are you?

Nora: (Suspiciously) How am I?

Mrs. Linden: I see you don't recognize me anymore.

Nora: Don't I? Oh, yes! That's right! (Suddenly becoming happy) What, Christine, is that really you?

Mrs. Linden: Yes, it's really me!

Nora: Christine, imagine, I didn't even recognize you! But I can't be blamed! (Lowering her voice) Christine, you really have changed!

Mrs. Linden: Yes, in these eight or nine years!

In the Carriage 209

— Zhuo Er

The weather is very hot, the capacity of the carriage is small, and there are many people, making it difficult to even breathe. Although every window is open, it is still suffocating, and I feel a bit dizzy! If you stick your head out of the car, it will be even worse. Coal ash flying from the front of the car will cover your face and body in black, and it might even get into your eyes, which would be even more uncomfortable. The passengers in the third-class carriage probably deserve this!

The train is crawling south step by step, naturally going further and further away from home. Due to nostalgia for home and unease about the unfamiliar new land, the feeling of being in a strange place is really uncomfortable, isn't it? Even the voices of the hawkers outside the station cannot be understood at all! It's like stepping into a foreign country. Everything is unfamiliar, unfamiliar. The only familiar things are the familiar natural scenery of the train and the lush green fields! Even so, at that time I seemed very conceited and said in a low voice: How vast and beautiful is the land that belongs to us! But, immediately there was a heavy blow, shattering this boastful illusion, that is: Half of the country has fallen into the hands of the enemy!

…My mood is drifting like gossamer, unable to be restrained, and like a ball of tangled hemp, unable to be quickly cleared. Fragments of memories swirl in my mind like a revolving lantern, and soon they lead me into an incomprehensible entanglement… I am tired. A new stimulus I received was the stiff-faced, self-important, and ugly attitude of that great citizen of a friendly nation sitting in the corner on the east side! His face is always raised, desperately raised, as if there is something noteworthy on the roof of the car!…

I don’t know when, I was accosted by a fellow villager and we started talking. He spoke so enthusiastically in our hometown dialect, and I felt like I had met a relative.

…“So, why did you go to Guandong?” I asked him again.

“Wasn’t it because I couldn’t stay at home anymore? You figure it out: drought followed by flooding, flooding followed by drought, war and chaos, bandits everywhere. How could I stay in my hometown? Who would want to leave their own home?” He said, and the word “bitter” was simply written on his face.

I, I also came from my hometown (but unlike him, I abandoned my hometown, not being driven away by it).

“What do you do in Guandong?”

“A poor person is poor wherever he goes! Anyway, I rely on my strength to eat!” He sighed deeply, “Everyone says you can get rich in Guandong! Get rich? How can someone like me who relies on physical labor get rich? That really has to wait for the sun to rise in the west!”

“How is Guandong now? Can the people live and work in peace?” (To be continued)

Lies 210

— (Blow)

Zhang Taiyan lectures in Wumen, extremely capable of attracting people. Jiang Kanghu lectures in Kanglu, also greatly advertising his propaganda. Tan Lao San said, one is the old store of Lu Gaojian who is starting out, one is the first house of Pu Wu who is a pioneer, I do not know whose business is thriving, God only knows. Or he said, it's boring, it's still more popular to sing big drums and Dongxiang tunes.

Rural villagers in southern Shandong organized the "Saintly and Virtuous Path" cult, exploited by a certain party. The military police went to search and arrest them. The villagers resisted. After three hours of fierce fighting, the ringleader was finally captured. Tan Lao San said, what kind of path is this? It is the path of reincarnation, the path of slavery, the path of national subjugation and the extermination of the race. When the saints and sages hear of this, they will surely shake their heads and stamp their feet endlessly.

Novel

Early Winter in Qingyang Port (10) 211

— Qiu Yuan

Zhuo Shi reached out his hand again, hugged her, and concentrated all his strength on her lips, deeply kissing Qiu Hua. Although, Zhuo Min had not never kissed a woman, but this kiss was not as pleasant as this one, not as meaningful as this one! After kissing, of course, they kissed again. This exchange of emotions transmitted through the lips, and the resonance of their pounding hearts, gave them a feeling that seemed even more sublime – a feeling that was more religious than emotional. He seemed to be in a tall and spacious Gothic church, with no one around, quietly. Qiu Hua seemed to have turned into Saint Mary. Zhuo Min had never experienced this sublime feeling before. Never before had a woman made him feel this sublime, somewhat religious, when Zhuo Min kissed her. For those women, the pleasure of kissing was limited to kissing, and if there was pleasure at all. He regarded them as women, and the kissing between men and women, in this kind of situation, also became a procedure rather than a rite. But today, as Zhuo Min kissed Qiu Hua, the tranquility in his heart was indescribable. He felt that what he had won was not only the love of a woman, he had found faith, found salvation, found the reason why life is precious as life. He savored Qiu Hua's words: "Of course, but we are different," which gave him even greater satisfaction in his heart.
